Jamison Brereton

51 (347)
Dawn
V─Бmadeva Gautama
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn is remarkable first for the fact that the dawns are always presented and addressed in the plural (тАЬDawnsтАЭ) rather than the singular, as so often. Indeed, when the poet wishes to refer to a single dawn, he uses instead the word тАЬlightтАЭ (vs. 1) or an unspecified pronoun (vs. 6). The grammatical plurality of the sub
ject Dawns serves a thematic purpose: as in other dawn hymns the poet notes that each dayтАЩs dawn is different, yet paradoxically all dawns are the same, coming in an unbroken chain from the east day after day (see, e.g., vs. 8).
As V. Yareham suggested (in an unpublished paper presented at the University of Texas Vedic Workshop, May 2007), the hymn is structured around an ompha los verse (6), with concentric matching verses surrounding it: 1тАУ2 / 10тАУ11 and 3тАУ5 / 7тАУ9. The omphalos poses a central and essentially unanswerable question, the one that always arises about the dawn(s): how can they be both the same and different, and the poet expresses his anxiety that he cannot identify the particular dawn in the swarm of identical ones. Behind this anxiety is another one, seen especially in verses 4, 6, and 7, namely whether we, the current sacrifi cers, will have the same material success with our dawn sacrifice as the ritualists of old.
Otherwise, the imagery is of the usual type for dawn hymns: the brilliant beauty of the dawns in contrast to the darkness, which they banish; their abrupt arising in the east and their subsequent journey; and the prayers for largesse, reminding us that the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б, the priestly gifts, were distributed at the dawn sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Dawn It is worth noting that the nom. (and voc.) pl. of uс╣г├бs- is consistently uс╣г├бsaс╕е in this hymn (every vs. but 10), with short suffixal vowel – the newer form replacing inherited uс╣г─Б╠Бsaс╕е.

As disc. in the published introduction, this is an omphalos hymn, with the middle verse 6 posing the central question. This omphalos is surrounded by concentric rings: div├│ duhit├бro vibh─Бt─л╠Бс╕е of 1c is answered by the same phrase (in the voc.) in 10a and 11a, while vss. 5 and 7 contain an inner ring with с╣Ыt├б- (с╣Ыtay├║bhiс╕е 5a, с╣Ыt├бj─Бtasaty─Бс╕е 7b) and sady├бс╕е (5b, 7d). There is also much lexical chaining between adjacent vss.

рдЗрджрдореБ рдкреБрд░рддреЛ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдорд┐рджрдВ рддреНрдпрддреН рддрджрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдВ рдкреБрд░реБрддрдордореН рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдГ рддреЗрдЬрдГ рд╡рдпреБрдирд╛рд╡рддреН рее рд╡реЗрддреЗрдГ рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдордг рдЗрджрдореН рее рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдорддреН ред рдЕрдерд╡рд╛ рд╡рдпреБрдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдо ред рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮреЛрдкреЗрддрдореН ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдХрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХреАрджреГрдХреН рддреЗрдЬрдГ ред рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВ рджрд┐рд╢рд┐ рддрдорд╕рдГ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рддреН рдЕрд╕реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЙрджрддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреН ред рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕рддрд┐ рдиреВрдирдВ рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рдЕрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рджреБрд╣рд┐рддрд░рдГ рджреБрд╣рд┐рддреГрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпрд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рддреАрдГ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреАрдГ рдЙрд╖рд╕реЛ рдЬрдирд╛рдп рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧрд╛рддреБрдВ рдЧрдордирдВ рдЧрдордирд╛рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрдВ рдХреГрдгрд╡рдиреН рдЕрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis widely-spread and sense-bestowing light has sprung up in the east from out of the darkness; verily the brilliant Dawns, the daughters of heaven, are giving to man (the faculty to act).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

G─Бtum kс╣Ыс╣Зavan jan─Бya = yajam─Бn─Бn─Бm gaman─Бdi vy─Бp─Бra s─Бmarthyam akurvan, they give to the offerer of sacrifice the ability to perform the acts such as going

Jamison Brereton

Here has this light, the latest of many, stood (up) out of the east from the darkness, with its patterns.
Now the daughters of Heaven radiating widely, the Dawns, will make a way for the people.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the dawns are so insistently in the plural in this hymn that when a single one is referred to, another word must be used – in this case jy├│tiс╕е тАШlightтАЩ.

Griffith

FORTH from the darkness in the region eastward this most abundant splendid light hatb mounted.
Now verily the far-refulgent Mornings, Daughters of Heaven, bring welfare to the people.

Geldner

Dort vorne im Osten ist dies Licht zum vielten Male der Finsternis entstiegen, die Zeiten machend. Nun sollen des Himmels T├╢chter, die Usas, durch ihr Erstrahlen dem Menschen den Weg bereiten.

Grassmann

Dies Licht erhob sich, das sich stets erneuet, mit hellem Schein im Osten aus dem Dunkel; Des Himmels Tochter, helle Morgenr├╢then, sie m├╢gen Wohlfahrt schaffen nun dem Menschen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe many-limbed Dawns rise up in the east, like the pillars plural nted at sacrifices (round the altar); radiant and purifying, they are manifested, opening the gates of the obstructing gloom.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

They have stood upтАФthe bright DawnsтАФin the east, like the sacrificial posts fixed at ceremonies.

They have unclosed the doors of the enclosure of darkness as they dawn, blazing and pure.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note absolute initial root aor. ├бsthuс╕е contrasting with absolute final asth─Бt in 1b.

I have taken gen. t├бmasaс╕е as dep. on gen. vraj├бsya (тАЬof the enclosure of darknessтАЭ) with Geldner, but t├бmasaс╕е could be dep. instead on dv─Б╠Бr─Б, parallel to vraj├бsya (so Renou, Witzel Got┼Н).

Griffith

The richly-coloured Dawns have mounted eastward, like pillars planted at our sacrifices,
And, flushing far, splendid and purifying, unbarred the portals of the fold of darkness.

Geldner

Die Usas stehen buntfarbig vorne im Osten da wie die aufgerichteten Pfosten bei den Opfern. Sie haben aufleuchtend die Tore des Pferchs der Finsternis aufgeschlossen, die Reinen, Hellen.

Grassmann

Im Ost erstanden lichte Morgenr├╢then, wie S├дulen, die beim Opfer aufgerichtet; Sie schlossen auf des dunkeln Stalles Th├╝ren aus eigner Lust, die flammenden, die hellen.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрджреНрдп рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рджрд┐рдиреЗ рдЙрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреАрдГ рддрдордГ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпрдиреНрддреНрдпрдГ рдордШреЛрдиреАрдГ рдзрдирд╡рддреНрдпрдГ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рднреЛрдЬрд╛рдиреН рднреЛрдЬрдпрд┐рддреДрдиреН рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд░рд╛рдзреЛрджреЗрдпрд╛рдп рд╕реЛрдорд╛рджрд┐рдзрдирджрд╛рдирд╛рдп рдЪрд┐рддрдпрдиреНрдд рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдЪрд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рдЕрдЪрд╛рдпрдиреАрдпреЗ рддрдорд╕реЛ рд╡рд┐рдордзреНрдпреЗ ред рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдЧрд╛рдврд╛рдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░реЗ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдкрдгрдпрдГ рд╡рдгрд┐рдЬ рдЗрд╡рд╛рджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдГ рдЕрдпреБрдзреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╕рд╕рдиреНрддреБ рд╕реНрд╡рдкрдиреНрддреБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gloom-dispelling, affluent Dawns animate the pious worshippers to offer (sacrificial) treasure; may the churlish (traffickers) sleep on unawakened, in the unlovely depth of darkness.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The churlish traffickers: paс╣Зaya = vaс╣Зijaс╕е, i.e., ad─Бt─Бraс╕е, non-givers

Jamison Brereton

Dawning today, the bounteous Dawns brighten the benefactors for the giving of largesse.
In (a place) without brightness let the niggards sleep, unawakening in the middle of darkness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The multivalent stem cit├бya- is here used in transitive value (see my disc. in

-├бya- book). The 3rd pl. citayanta is simply an -anta replacement of the expected active of the usual type (see my 1979 IIJ article).

Griffith

Dispelling gloom this day the wealthy Mornings urge liberal givers to present their treasures.
In the unlightened depth of darkness round them let niggard traffickers sleep unawakened.

Geldner

Bei ihrem Hellwerden m├╢gen die gabenreichen Usas┬┤ heute die Freigebigen erleuchten, auf da├Я sie Belohnung gew├дhren. Im Unerhellten sollen die Knauser weiter schlafen, ohne zu erwachen, ganz im Finstern.

Grassmann

Sie m├╢gen willig heut die Spender reizen zum Schatzverleihn, die reichen Morgenr├╢then; Im finstern Raume lasst die Geiz’gen schlafen, sie nicht erwachen in des Dunkels Mitte.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine Dawns, may your chariot, whether old or new, be frequent at this day’s (worship), wherewith, affluent Dawns, possessing riches, (you shine) upon the seven-mouthed (troop of the) Aс╣Еgirasas, the observers of the nine or ten days’ rite.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seven-mouthed aс╣Еgirasas: repeating the seven vedic metres; nine or ten days rites: cf. RV. 10.62.6

Jamison Brereton

Goddess Dawns, should it be the old course or a new one for you todayтАФ
(or the one going) along which, you rich ladies, you richly dawned on the Aс╣Еgiras(-clan) of the Nine-Cows, of the Ten-Cows, of the Seven-Mouths?

Jamison Brereton Notes

The opening of this vs. kuv├нt s├б resonates with the opening of 6 с╕▒u va svid.

With Geldner I take the y├йn─Б clause of cd to be a third possible course, against the old and new ones offered as possibilities in ab. Since cd presumably refers to the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ involvement in the Vala myth, it is the case that the DawnsтАЩ course in that instance was an unusual one: they came out of a rock!

Griffith

O Goddesses, is this your car, I ask you, ancient this day, or is it new, ye Mornings,
Wherewith, rich Dawns, ye seek with wealth Navagva, Dasagva Angira, the seven-toned singer?

Ob dies wohl heute eure alte oder eine neue Fahrt sein mag, ihr g├╢ttlichen Usas┬┤, ob dieselbe, auf dem ihr ├╝ber Navagva, Angira, Dasagva mit siebenfachem Munde, Reichtum bringend, ihr Reichen, aufgegangen seid?

English translation:

тАЬDivine Dawns, with horses that frequent sacrifices you quickly travel round the regions (of space); awake the sleeping being, whether biped or quadruped, to pursue (his functions).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you, goddesses, with horses whose yoke is truth, drive around the creatures in a single day,
awakening the sleeping, every two-footed and four-footed living thing, to activity, o Dawns.

Griffith

With horses harnessed by eternal Order, Goddesses, swiftly round the worlds ye travel,
Arousing from their rest, O Dawns, the sleeping, and all that lives, man, bird, and beast, to motion.

Geldner

Grassmann

Denn ihr G├╢ttinnen fahrt in einem Tage rings um die Welt mit gutgeschirrten Rossen, Den Schlafenden erweckend, Morgenr├╢then, und was da lebt zum Wandern, Thier und Menschen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhere is that ancient one of those (Dawns), through whom the works of the с╣Ъbhus were accomplished? For as the bright Dawns happily proceed, they are not distinguished, being alike and undecaying.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Where is she, which one of them is she, the age-old one along with whom they distributed the distributions of the
R╠еbhus?
(I ask because) when the beautiful Dawns proceed in beauty, they cannot be distinguishedтАФthe unaging ones having the same
appearance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

katam─Б╠БтАШwhich one?тАЩ echoes purut├бmam тАШthe latest of manyтАЩ in 1a. Note that again when a singular dawn is referred to, the word uс╣г├бs- is not used.

I do not understand what the с╣Ъbhus are doing here, nor do I know the exact sense of v├н тИЪdh─Б in the etymological figure vidh─Б╠Бn─Б vidadh├║с╕е. A similar etym. figure is found in nearby IV.55.2 vidh─Бt─Б╠Бro v├н тАж dadhuс╕е, where I tr. тАШdistributeтАЩ, which IтАЩve imported here. However, I am now inclined to think that this has to do with the creative division of an undifferentiated mass (such as the с╣Ъbhus performed in I.161.2-3 also cited by Geldner) and with the regulation of these divisions, possibly of divisions of time. Such тАЬdivisionтАЭ contrasts sharply with the lack of distinction among the dawns stated in cd. It is not surprising that a single (unnamed) dawn (p─Бda a) would be associated with division and distinction (p─Бda b), as opposed to the plural dawns in the rest of the hymn. For other interpr. of p─Бda b see the various tr. and comm. _________ 07
The opening t─Б╠Б, esp. in its emphatic form t─Б╠Бgh─Б t─Б╠Б(с╕е) is echoed by the openings of 8 (t─Б╠Б─Б╠БтАж) and 9 (t─Б╠Б(с╕е)).

At the same time sady├бс╕е makes an interior ring with 5b around the omphalos vs. What’s striking about this little ring is that, though the sady├бс╕е in 5 and 7 match verbally, the word is in a different temporal setting in the two vss: present in 5 and remote past in 7, and in 6 those two temporal settings are dissolved or confused (as also in a different way in 4).

The cmpd. с╣Ыt├бj─Бtasatya- is unusual not only in having 3 members (quite rare in the RV) but also for containing both с╣Ыt├б- and saty├б-. Renou suggests that -satyafunctions as a sort of тАЬparticule intensive.тАЭ Given how charged both words are in the RV, I think this unlikely, although the rendering in the published translation (тАЬwho were really born of truthтАЭ) is close to RenouтАЩs intensive particle interpr; cf. his own tr.

(тАЬv├йritablement n├йes de lтАЩOrdreтАЭ). I think the cmpd requires a more literal and weighty rendering – тАЬwhose reality was born from truthтАЭ (which I would substitute for what is found in the published translation) – meaning that the dawns we see and who come daily to our world and our sacrifice, who are really here, arose from the true cosmic patterns that govern the universe of time and space.

Griffith

Which among these is eldest, and where is she through whom they fixed the Rbhus’ regulations?
What time the splendid Dawns go forth for splendour, they are not known aparto alike, unwasting.

рддрд╛ рдШ ред рдШреЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреМ ред рддрд╛рдГ рдЦрд▓реВрдкрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреНрдпрдГ рддрд╛ рднрджреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгреНрдпрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдореН рдЖрд╕реБрдГ рдЕрднрд╡рдиреН ред рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирд╛рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдордирдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗрдг рджреНрдпреБрдореНрдирдВ рдзрдирдВ рдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдВ рддрд╛рдГ ред рдЛрддрдЬрд╛рддрд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рдЛрддрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдЬрд╛рддрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддрд╛рдГ рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рддреНрдпрдлрд▓рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдГ ред рдпрд╛рд╕реБ рдЙрд╖рдГрд╕реБ рдИрдЬрд╛рдирдГ рдпрд╛рдЧрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрдГ рдЙрдХреНрдереИрдГ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реИрдГ рд╢рд╢рдорд╛рдирдГ рд╢рдВрд╕рдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреН рд╕рд╛рдорднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рдВ рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрд╛рджрдпрдиреН рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреН рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рдгрдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╕рджреНрдпрдГ рдЖрдк рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рддрд╛ рднрджреНрд░рд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVerily those auspicious Dawns have been of old, rich with desired blessings, truthful (bestowers) of the results of sacrifice; at which the sacrificer, adoring with (silent) praise, glorifying (with hymns), has quickly obtained wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These same auspicious Dawns existed of old, those of superior heavenliness, who were really born of truth,
at whose (time) one who had sacrificed and labored with
hymns, praising and chanting, reached wealth in a single
day.

Griffith

Blest were these Dawns of old, shining with succour, true with the truth that springs from holy Order;
With whom the toiling worshipper, by praises, hymning and lauding, soon attained to riches.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey spread around of smilar form, (coming) from the east, (coming) from the same region alike renowned; the divine Dawns, arousing the assembly of the sacrifice are glorified like the (rays) creative of the waters.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rays: gav─Бm sarg─Б na ra┼Ыmayaс╕е: RV. 4.52.5

Jamison Brereton

They proceed, in the same way, from the east, spreading out from the same place in the same way.
The Goddess Dawns, awakening from the seat of truth, like gushes of cows, become wakeful. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Jamison Brereton Notes

The unbroken similarity of the dawns who just keep coming, day after day, is conveyed by the stasis of these two vss., where forms of тАШsameтАЩ (8ab saman─Б╠Б тАж san─Бn├бtaс╕е samany─Б╠Б, 9a saman─Б╠Бsam─Бn─л╠Бс╕е) and the same verb caranti (8a, 9b) bring all movement to a halt, even though the dawns are constantly on the move.

Griffith

Hither from eastward all at once they travel, from one place spreading in the selfsame manner.
Awaking, from the seat of holy Order the Godlike Dawns come nigh like troops of cattle.

Geldner

Sie kommen gleichm├д├Яig aus Osten, von der gleichen Stelle aus gleichm├д├Яig sich ausbreitend. Vom Sitze der Ordnung erwacht sind die G├╢ttinnen Usas┬┤ fr├╝h munter wie die Schw├дrme der K├╝he.

Grassmann

Sie wandern herw├дrts allzumal von Osten auf gleiche Weise allesammt sich breitend, Die G├╢ttlichen, aus heil’gem Sitz erwachend, die Morgenr├╢then nahn wie Heerden K├╝he.

English translation:

тАЬThose Dawns proceed verily all alike, of similar form, of infinite hues, pure, bright, illumining, concealing by their radiant person ns the very great gloom.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just these nowтАФthe same ones in the same wayтАФwith immutable colors, the Dawns proceed,
hiding the black void with their bright (colors), glistening, gleaming, shining with their own bodies. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The unbroken similarity of the dawns who just keep coming, day after day, is conveyed by the stasis of these two vss., where forms of тАШsameтАЩ (8ab saman─Б╠Б тАж san─Бn├бtaс╕е samany─Б╠Б, 9a saman─Б╠Бsam─Бn─л╠Бс╕е) and the same verb caranti (8a, 9b) bring all movement to a halt, even though the dawns are constantly on the move.

Griffith

Thus they go forth with undiminished colours, these Mornings similar, in self-same fashion,
Concealing the gigantic might of darkness with radiant bodies bright and pure and shining.

Geldner

Dieselben Usas┬┤ wandeln in gleicher Weise sich gleichend mit unver├дnderter Farbe, indem sie das schwarze Ungeheuer mit ihren hellen Farben beseitigen, die hellen, am Leibe reinen, gl├дnzenden.

Grassmann

So wandern sie auf gleiche Art, sich ├дhnlich, die Morgenr├╢then, nicht die Farbe wechselnd, Das grause Dunkel durch die Strahlen bergend, an Leibern strahlend, schimmernd hell und gl├дnzend.

Elizarenkova

тАЬDivine, resplendent daughters of heaven, bestow upon us wealth, comprehending progeny; awaking you for our benefit, may we be the lords of excellent descendants.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O daughters of Heaven, radiating widely, bestow on us wealth in offspring, o goddesses.
Being awakened from a comfortable place in response to you, may we be lords of an abundance of heroes.

Griffith

O Goddesses, O Heaven’s refulgent Daughters, bestow upon us wealth with store of children.
As from our pleasant place of rest ye rouse us may we be masters of heroic vigour.

English translation:

тАЬDaughters of heaven, resplendent Dawns, I address you (as) the announcer of the sacrificer; may we be (the possessors) of celebrity among men, and may heaven and the divine earth perpetuate (it).тАЭ

The verse is to be inaudibly recited every morning at day-break

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддрддреН) (рд╡рдГ) рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╕реНрдп (рджреБрд╣рд┐рддрд░рдГ) рдХрдиреНрдпрд╛ рдЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ (рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рддреАрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрдиреНрддреНрдпрдГ (рдЙрдк) (рдмреНрд░реБрд╡реЗ) рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢рд╛рдорд┐ (рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░реНрд╡реЗрд▓рд╛рдпрд╛рдГ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдХреЗрддреБрдГ) рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХрдГ (рд╡рдпрдореН) (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) (рдпрд╢рд╕рдГ) рдпрд╢рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдГ (рдЬрдиреЗрд╖реБ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕реБ (рддрддреН) (рджреНрдпреМрдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддреН (рдЪ) (рдзрддреНрддрд╛рдореН) (рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) (рдЪ) (рджреЗрд╡реА) рджреЗрджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпреЗ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╛рдиреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдп рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдХрд╛ рднреВрдорд┐рд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдзрд░реНрддреНрддрд╛рд░реЛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрд╖рдГрд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ реерезрезрее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рдзрд┐рдХрдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреЗ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░реВрди рд╕рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреЗ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рдд рддреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдХ рд╡ рднреВрдореАрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрд▓рд╛ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд░реЗ рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд. рее резрез рее
